This implementation does not guarantee that only one\n    20→// client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\n    21→//\n    22→// A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\n    23→// leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\n    24→// election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\n    25→// produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\n    26→// accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\n    27→// renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\n    28→// clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\n    29→//\n    30→// However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\n    31→// RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\n    32→// maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\n    33→// the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\n    34→// the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\n    35→// to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n    36→// the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n    37→//\n    38→// While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n    39→// cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\n    40→// this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\n    41→// availability.\n    42→//\n    43→// Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\n    44→// taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\n    45→// should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\n    46→// until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\n    47→// when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\n    48→// to master availability.\n    49→//\n    50→// DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This library will likely change significantly\n    51→// or even be removed entirely in subsequent releases. Depend on this API at\n    52→// your own risk.\n    53→package leaderelection\n    54→\n    55→import (\n    56→\t\"bytes\"\n    57→\t\"context\"\n    58→\t\"fmt\"\n    59→\t\"sync\"\n 71→const (\n    72→\tJitterFactor = 1.2\n    73→)\n    74→\n    75→// NewLeaderElector creates a LeaderElector from a LeaderElectionConfig\n    76→func NewLeaderElector(lec LeaderElectionConfig) (*LeaderElector, error) {\n    77→\tif lec.LeaseDuration <= lec.RenewDeadline {\n    78→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"leaseDuration must be greater than renewDeadline\")\n    79→\t}\n    80→\tif 108→\t\tconfig:  lec,\n   109→\t\tclock:   clock.RealClock{},\n   110→\t\tmetrics: globalMetricsFactory.newLeaderMetrics(),\n   111→\t}\n   112→\tle.metrics.leaderOff(le.config.Name)\n   113→\treturn &le, nil\n   114→}\n   115→\n   116→type LeaderElectionConfig struct {\n   117→\t// Lock is the resource that will be used for locking\n   118→\tLock rl.Interface\n   119→\n   120→\t// LeaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will\n   121→\t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\n   122→\t// last observed ack.\n   123→\t//\n   124→\t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\n   125→\t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\n   126→\t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\n   127→\t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\n   128→\t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\n   129→\t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\n   130→\t// long waits in the scenario.\n   131→\t//\n   132→\t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\n   133→\tLeaseDuration time.Duration\n   134→\t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\n   135→\t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\n   136→\t//\n   137→\t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\n   138→\tRenewDeadline time.Duration\n   139→\t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\n   140→\t// between tries of actions.\n   141→\t//\n   142→\t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\n   143→\tRetryPeriod time.Duration\n   144→\n   145→\t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\n   146→\t// events of the LeaderElector\n   147→\tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\n   148→\n   149→\t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\n   150→\t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\n   151→\tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\n   152→\n   153→\t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\n   154→\t// when the run context is cancelled. If you set this to true, you must\n   155→\t// ensure all code guarded by this lease has successfully completed\n   156→\t// prior to cancelling the context, or you may have two processes\n   157→\t// simultaneously acting on the critical path.\n   158→\tReleaseOnCancel bool\n   159→\n   160→\t// Name is the name of the resource lock for debugging\n   161→\tName string\n   162→\n   163→\t// Coordinated will use the Coordinated Leader Election feature\n   164→\t// WARNING: Coordinated leader election is ALPHA.\n   165→\tCoordinated bool\n   166→}\n   167→\n   168→// LeaderCallbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain\n   169→// lifecycle events of the LeaderElector. These are invoked asynchronously.\n   170→//\n   171→// possible future callbacks:\n   172→//   - OnChallenge()\n   173→type LeaderCallbacks struct {\n   174→\t// OnStartedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client starts leading\n   175→\tOnStartedLeading func(context.Context)\n   176→\t// OnStoppedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client stops leading.\n   177→\t// This callback is always called when the LeaderElector exits, even if it did not start leading.\n   178→\t// Users should not assume that OnStoppedLeading is only called after OnStartedLeading.\n   179→\t// see: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/127675#discussion_r1780059887\n   180→\tOnStoppedLeading func()\n   181→\t// OnNewLeader is called when the client observes a leader that is\n   182→\t// not the previously observed leader. This includes the first observed\n   183→\t// leader when the client starts.\n   184→\tOnNewLeader func(identity string)\n   185→}\n   186→\n   187→// LeaderElector is a leader election client.\n   188→type LeaderElector struct {\n   189→\tconfig LeaderElectionConfig\n   190→\t// internal bookkeeping\n   191→\tobservedRecord    rl.LeaderElectionRecord\n   192→\tobservedRawRecord []byte\n   193→\tobservedTime      time.Time\n   194→\t// used to implement OnNewLeader(), may lag slightly from the\n   195→\t// value observedRecord.HolderIdentity if the transition has\n   196→\t// not yet been reported.\n   197→\treportedLeader string\n   198→\n   199→\t// clock is wrapper around time to allow for less flaky testing\n   200→\tclock clock.Clock\n   201→\n   202→\t// used to lock the observedRecord and the observedTime\n   203→\tobservedRecordLock sync.RWMutex\n   204→\n   205→\tmetrics leaderMetricsAdapter\n   206→}\n   207→\n   208→// Run starts the leader election loop. Run will not return\n   209→// before leader election loop is stopped by ctx or it has\n   210→// stopped holding the leader lease\n   211→func (le *LeaderElector) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n   212→\tdefer runtime.HandleCrashWithContext(ctx)\n   213→\tdefer le.config.Callbacks.OnStoppedLeading()\n   214→\n   215→\tif !le.acquire(ctx) {\n   216→\t\treturn // ctx signalled done\n   217→\t}\n   218→\tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n   219→\tdefer cancel()\n   220→\tgo le.config.Callbacks.OnStartedLeading(ctx)\n   221→\tle.renew(ctx)\n   222→}\n   223→\n   224→// RunOrDie starts a client with the provided config or panics if the config\n   225→// fails to validate. RunOrDie blocks until leader election loop is\n   226→// stopped by ctx or it has stopped holding the leader lease\n   227→func RunOrDie(ctx context.Context, lec LeaderElectionConfig) {\n   228→\tle, err := NewLeaderElector(lec)\n   229→\tif err != nil {\n   230→\t\tpanic(err)\n   231→\t}\n   232→\tif lec.WatchDog != nil {\n   233→\t\tlec.WatchDog.SetLeaderElection(le)\n   234→\t}\n   235→\tle.Run(ctx)\n   236→}\n   237→\n   238→// GetLeader returns the identity of the last observed leader or returns the empty string if\n   239→// no leader has yet been observed.\n   240→// This function is for informational purposes. last observed leader was this client else returns false.\n   246→func (le *LeaderElector) IsLeader() bool {\n   247→\treturn le.getObservedRecord().HolderIdentity == le.config.Lock.Identity()\n   248→}\n   249→\n   250→// acquire loops calling tryAcquireOrRenew and returns true immediately when tryAcquireOrRenew succeeds.\n   251→// Returns false if ctx signals done.\n   252→func (le *LeaderElector) acquire(ctx context.Context) bool {\n   253→\tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n   254→\tdefer cancel()\n   255→\tsucceeded := false\n   256→\tdesc := le.config.Lock.Describe()\n   257→\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n   258→\tlogger.Info(\"Attempting to acquire leader lease...\", \"lock\", desc)\n   259→\twait.JitterUntilWithContext(ctx, func(ctx context.Context) {\n 265→\t\tle.maybeReportTransition()\n   266→\t\tif !succeeded {\n   267→\t\t\tlogger.V(4).Info(\"Failed to acquire lease\", \"lock\", desc)\n   268→\t\t\treturn\n   269→\t\t}\n or ctx signals done.\n   279→func (le *LeaderElector) renew(ctx context.Context) {\n   280→\tdefer le.config.Lock.RecordEvent(\"stopped leading\")\n   281→\tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n   282→\tdefer cancel()\n   283→\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n   284→\twait.UntilWithContext(ctx, func(ctx context.Context) {\n   285→\t\terr := wait.PollUntilContextTimeout(ctx, when immediate=true.\n   287→\t\t\t// Short-circuit this to prevent unnecessary processing and error log messages.\n   288→\t\t\tif err := ctx.Err(); err != nil {\n   289→\t\t\t\treturn false, err\n lease\", \"lock\", desc)\n   301→\t\t\treturn\n   302→\t\t}\n   303→\t\tle.metrics.leaderOff(le.config.Name)\n   304→\t\tlogger.Info(\"Failed to renew lease\", \"lock\", desc, \"err\", err)\n 312→}\n   313→\n   314→// release attempts to release the leader lease if we have acquired it.\n   315→func (le *LeaderElector) release(logger klog.Logger) bool {\n   316→\tctx := and tries to renew the\n   350→// lease if it has already been acquired. Returns true on success else returns\n   351→// false.\n   352→func (le *LeaderElector) tryCoordinatedRenew(ctx context.Context) bool {\n   353→\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n   354→\tnow := metav1.NewTime(le.clock.Now())\n   355→\tleaderElectionRecord := rl.LeaderElectionRecord{\n   356→\t\tHolderIdentity:       le.config.Lock.Identity(),\n   357→\t\tLeaseDurationSeconds: int(le.config.LeaseDuration / time.Second),\n   358→\t\tRenewTime:            now,\n   359→\t\tAcquireTime:          now,\n   360→\t}\n   361→\n   362→\t// 1. obtain the electionRecord\n   363→\toldLeaderElectionRecord, oldLeaderElectionRawRecord, err := le.config.Lock.Get(ctx)\n   364→\tif err != nil {\n   365→\t\tif !errors.IsNotFound(err) {\n   366→\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Error retrieving lease lock\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\n   367→\t\t\treturn false\n   368→\t\t}\n   369→\t\tlogger.Info(\"Lease lock not found\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe(), \"err\", err)\n   370→\t\treturn false\n   371→\t}\n   372→\n   373→\t// 2. If the lease has been marked as \"end of term\", don't renew it\n   396→\tif le.IsLeader() && oldLeaderElectionRecord.PreferredHolder != \"\" {\n   397→\t\tlogger.V(4).Info(\"Lease is marked as 'end of term'\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\n   398→\t\t// TODO: Instead of letting lease expire, the holder may deleted it directly\n   399→\t\t// This will not be compatible with all controllers, so it needs to be opt-in behavior.\n   400→\t\t// We must ensure all code guarded by this lease has successfully completed\n   401→\t\t// prior to releasing or there may be two processes\n   402→\t\t// simultaneously acting on the critical path.\n   403→\t\t// Usually once this returns false, the process is terminated..\n   404→\t\t// xref: OnStoppedLeading\n   405→\t\treturn false\n   406→\t}\n   407→\n   408→\t// 3. Returns true\n   431→// on success else returns false.\n   432→func (le *LeaderElector) tryAcquireOrRenew(ctx context.Context) bool {\n   433→\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n   434→\tnow := metav1.NewTime(le.clock.Now())\n   435→\tleaderElectionRecord := rl.LeaderElectionRecord{\n   436→\t\tHolderIdentity:       le.config.Lock.Identity(),\n   437→\t\tLeaseDurationSeconds: int(le.config.LeaseDuration / time.Second),\n   438→\t\tRenewTime:            now,\n   439→\t\tAcquireTime:          now,\n   440→\t}\n   441→\n   442→\t// 1. fast path for the leader to update optimistically assuming that the record observed\n   443→\t// last time is the current version.\n   444→\tif le.IsLeader() && le.isLeaseValid(now.Time) {\n   445→\t\toldObservedRecord := le.getObservedRecord()\n   446→\t\tleaderElectionRecord.AcquireTime = oldObservedRecord.AcquireTime\n   447→\t\tleaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions = oldObservedRecord.LeaderTransitions\n   448→\n   449→\t\terr := le.config.Lock.Update(ctx, leaderElectionRecord)\n   450→\t\tif err == nil {\n   451→\t\t\tle.setObservedRecord(&leaderElectionRecord)\n   452→\t\t\treturn true\n   453→\t\t}\n   454→\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Failed to update lease optimistically, falling back to slow path\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\n   455→\t}\n   456→\n   457→\t// 2. obtain or create the ElectionRecord\n   458→\toldLeaderElectionRecord, oldLeaderElectionRawRecord, err := le.config.Lock.Get(ctx)\n   459→\tif err != nil {\n   460→\t\tif !errors.IsNotFound(err) {\n   461→\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Error retrieving lease lock\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\n   462→\t\t\treturn false\n   463→\t\t}\n   464→\t\tif err = le.config.Lock.Create(ctx, leaderElectionRecord); This implementation does not guarantee that only one\n// client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\n//\n// A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\n// leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\n// election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\n// produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\n// accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\n// renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\n// clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\n//\n// However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\n// RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\n// maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\n// the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\n// the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\n// to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n// the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n//\n// While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n// cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\n// this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\n// availability.\n//\n// Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\n// taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\n// should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\n// until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\n// when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\n// to master availability.\n//\n// DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This library will likely change significantly\n// or even be removed entirely in subsequent releases. Depend on this API at\n// your own risk.\npackage leaderelection\n\nimport (\n\t\"bytes\"\n\t\"context\"\n\t\"fmt\"\n\t\"sync\"\n\t\"time\"\n\n\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/errors\"\n\tmetav1 \"k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock\"\n\t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n\t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n)\n\nconst (\n\tJitterFactor = 1.2\n)\n\n// NewLeaderElector creates a LeaderElector from a LeaderElectionConfig\nfunc NewLeaderElector(lec LeaderElectionConfig) (*LeaderElector, error) {\n\tif lec.LeaseDuration <= lec.RenewDeadline {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"leaseDuration must be greater than renewDeadline\")\n\t}\n\tif lec.RenewDeadline <= time.Duration(JitterFactor*float64(lec.RetryPeriod)) {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"renewDeadline must be greater than retryPeriod*JitterFactor\")\n\t}\n\tif lec.LeaseDuration < 1 {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"leaseDuration must be greater than zero\")\n\t}\n\tif lec.RenewDeadline < 1 {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"renewDeadline must be greater than zero\")\n\t}\n\tif lec.RetryPeriod < 1 {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"retryPeriod must be greater than zero\")\n\t}\n\tif {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"Lock identity is empty\")\n\t}\n\n\tle := LeaderElector{\n\t\tconfig:  lec,\n\t\tclock:   clock.RealClock{},\n\t\tmetrics: globalMetricsFactory.newLeaderMetrics(),\n\t}\n\tle.metrics.leaderOff(le.config.Name)\n\treturn &le, nil\n}\n\ntype LeaderElectionConfig struct {\n\t// Lock is the resource that will be used for locking\n\tLock rl.Interface\n\n\t// LeaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will\n\t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\n\t// last observed ack.\n\t//\n\t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\n\t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\n\t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\n\t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\n\t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\n\t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\n\t// long waits in the scenario.\n\t//\n\t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\n\tLeaseDuration time.Duration\n\t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\n\t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\n\t//\n\t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\n\tRenewDeadline time.Duration\n\t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\n\t// between tries of actions.\n\t//\n\t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\n\tRetryPeriod time.Duration\n\n\t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\n\t// events of the LeaderElector\n\tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\n\n\t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\n\t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\n\tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\n\n\t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\n\t// when the run context is cancelled. If you set this to true, you must\n\t// ensure all code guarded by this lease has successfully completed\n\t// prior to cancelling the context, or you may have two processes\n\t// simultaneously acting on the critical path.\n\tReleaseOnCancel bool\n\n\t// Name is the name of the resource lock for debugging\n\tName string\n\n\t// Coordinated will use the Coordinated Leader Election feature\n\t// WARNING: Coordinated leader election is ALPHA.\n\tCoordinated bool\n}\n\n// LeaderCallbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain\n// lifecycle events of the LeaderElector. These are invoked asynchronously.\n//\n// possible future callbacks:\n//   - OnChallenge()\ntype LeaderCallbacks struct {\n\t// OnStartedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client starts leading\n\tOnStartedLeading func(context.Context)\n\t// OnStoppedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client stops leading.\n\t// This callback is always called when the LeaderElector exits, even if it did not start leading.\n\t// Users should not assume that OnStoppedLeading is only called after OnStartedLeading.\n\t// see: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/127675#discussion_r1780059887\n\tOnStoppedLeading func()\n\t// OnNewLeader is called when the client observes a leader that is\n\t// not the previously observed leader. This includes the first observed\n\t// leader when the client starts.\n\tOnNewLeader func(identity string)\n}\n\n// LeaderElector is a leader election client.\ntype LeaderElector struct {\n\tconfig LeaderElectionConfig\n\t// internal bookkeeping\n\tobservedRecord    rl.LeaderElectionRecord\n\tobservedRawRecord []byte\n\tobservedTime      time.Time\n\t// used to implement OnNewLeader(), may lag slightly from the\n\t// value observedRecord.HolderIdentity if the transition has\n\t// not yet been reported.\n\treportedLeader string\n\n\t// clock is wrapper around time to allow for less flaky testing\n\tclock clock.Clock\n\n\t// used to lock the observedRecord and the observedTime\n\tobservedRecordLock sync.RWMutex\n\n\tmetrics leaderMetricsAdapter\n}\n\n// Run starts the leader election loop. Run will not return\n// before leader election loop is stopped by ctx or it has\n// stopped holding the leader lease\nfunc (le *LeaderElector) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n\tdefer runtime.HandleCrashWithContext(ctx)\n\tdefer le.config.Callbacks.OnStoppedLeading()\n\n\tif !le.acquire(ctx) {\n\t\treturn // ctx signalled done\n\t}\n\tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n\tdefer cancel()\n\tgo le.config.Callbacks.OnStartedLeading(ctx)\n\tle.renew(ctx)\n}\n\n// RunOrDie starts a client with the provided config or panics if the config\n// fails to validate. RunOrDie blocks until leader election loop is\n// stopped by ctx or it has stopped holding the leader lease\nfunc RunOrDie(ctx context.Context, lec LeaderElectionConfig) {\n\tle, err := NewLeaderElector(lec)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tpanic(err)\n\t}\n\tif lec.WatchDog != nil {\n\t\tlec.WatchDog.SetLeaderElection(le)\n\t}\n\tle.Run(ctx)\n}\n\n// GetLeader returns the identity of the last observed leader or returns the empty string if\n// no leader has yet been observed.\n// This function is for informational purposes. (e.g. monitoring, logs, etc.)\nfunc (le *LeaderElector) GetLeader() string {\n\treturn le.getObservedRecord().HolderIdentity\n}\n\n// IsLeader returns true if the last observed leader was this client else returns false.\nfunc (le *LeaderElector) IsLeader() bool {\n\treturn le.getObservedRecord().HolderIdentity == le.config.Lock.Identity()\n}\n\n// acquire loops calling tryAcquireOrRenew and returns true immediately when tryAcquireOrRenew succeeds.\n// Returns false if ctx signals done.\nfunc (le *LeaderElector) acquire(ctx context.Context) bool {\n\tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n\tdefer cancel()\n\tsucceeded := false\n\tdesc := le.config.Lock.Describe()\n\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n\tlogger.Info(\"Attempting to acquire leader lease...\", \"lock\", desc)\n\twait.JitterUntilWithContext(ctx, func(ctx context.Context) {\n\t\tif !le.config.Coordinated {\n\t\t\tsucceeded = le.tryAcquireOrRenew(ctx)\n\t\t} else {\n\t\t\tsucceeded = le.tryCoordinatedRenew(ctx)\n\t\t}\n\t\tle.maybeReportTransition()\n\t\tif !succeeded {\n\t\t\tlogger.V(4).Info(\"Failed to acquire lease\", \"lock\", desc)\n\t\t\treturn\n\t\t}\n\t\tle.config.Lock.RecordEvent(\"became leader\")\n\t\tle.metrics.leaderOn(le.config.Name)\n\t\tlogger.Info(\"Successfully acquired lease\", \"lock\", desc)\n\t\tcancel()\n\t}, le.config.RetryPeriod, JitterFactor, true)\n\treturn succeeded\n}\n\n// renew loops calling tryAcquireOrRenew and returns immediately when tryAcquireOrRenew fails or ctx signals done.\nfunc (le *LeaderElector) renew(ctx context.Context) {\n\tdefer le.config.Lock.RecordEvent(\"stopped leading\")\n\tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n\tdefer cancel()\n\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n\twait.UntilWithContext(ctx, func(ctx context.Context) {\n\t\terr := wait.PollUntilContextTimeout(ctx, le.config.RetryPeriod, le.config.RenewDeadline, true, func(ctx processing and error log messages.\n\t\t\tif err := ctx.Err(); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn false, err\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif !le.config.Coordinated {\n\t\t\t\treturn le.tryAcquireOrRenew(ctx), {\n\t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Successfully renewed lease\", \"lock\", desc)\n\t\t\treturn\n\t\t}\n\t\tle.metrics.leaderOff(le.config.Name)\n\t\tlogger.Info(\"Failed to renew lease\", \"lock\", desc, \"err\", err)\n\t\tcancel()\n\t}, le.config.RetryPeriod)\n\n\t// if we hold the lease, give it up\n\tif le.config.ReleaseOnCancel {\n\t\tle.release(logger)\n\t}\n}\n\n// release attempts to release the leader lease if we have acquired it.\nfunc (le *LeaderElector) release(logger klog.Logger) bool {\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\ttimeoutCtx, timeoutCancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, le.config.RenewDeadline)\n\tdefer timeoutCancel()\n\t// update the resourceVersion of lease\n\toldLeaderElectionRecord, _, err := le.config.Lock.Get(timeoutCtx)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tif !errors.IsNotFound(err) {\n\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"error retrieving resource lock\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t\tlogger.Info(\"lease lock not found\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\n\tif !le.IsLeader() {\n\t\treturn true\n\t}\n\tnow := metav1.NewTime(le.clock.Now())\n\tleaderElectionRecord := false\n\t}\n\n\tle.setObservedRecord(&leaderElectionRecord)\n\treturn true\n}\n\n// tryCoordinatedRenew checks if it acquired a lease and tries to renew the\n// lease if it has already been acquired. Returns true on success else returns\n// false.\nfunc (le *LeaderElector) tryCoordinatedRenew(ctx context.Context) bool {\n\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n\tnow := metav1.NewTime(le.clock.Now())\n\tleaderElectionRecord := rl.LeaderElectionRecord{\n\t\tHolderIdentity:       le.config.Lock.Identity(),\n\t\tLeaseDurationSeconds: int(le.config.LeaseDuration / time.Second),\n\t\tRenewTime:            now,\n\t\tAcquireTime:          now,\n\t}\n\n\t// 1. obtain the electionRecord\n\toldLeaderElectionRecord, oldLeaderElectionRawRecord, err := le.config.Lock.Get(ctx)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tif !errors.IsNotFound(err) {\n\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Error retrieving lease lock\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t\tlogger.Info(\"Lease lock not found\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe(), \"err\", err)\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\n\t// 2. If the lease has been marked as \"end of term\", don't renew it\n\tif le.IsLeader() && oldLeaderElectionRecord.PreferredHolder != \"\" {\n\t\tlogger.V(4).Info(\"Lease is marked as 'end of term'\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\n\t\t// TODO: Instead of letting lease expire, the holder may deleted it directly\n\t\t// This will not be compatible with all controllers, so it needs to be opt-in behavior.\n\t\t// We must ensure all code guarded by this lease has successfully completed\n\t\t// prior to releasing or there may be two processes\n\t\t// simultaneously acting on the critical path.\n\t\t// Usually once this returns false, the process is terminated..\n\t\t// xref: OnStoppedLeading\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\n\t// 3. Let's correct it before updating.\n\tif le.IsLeader() {\n\t\tleaderElectionRecord.AcquireTime = oldLeaderElectionRecord.AcquireTime\n\t\tleaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions = oldLeaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions\n\t\tleaderElectionRecord.Strategy = oldLeaderElectionRecord.Strategy\n\t\tle.metrics.slowpathExercised(le.config.Name)\n\t} else {\n\t\tleaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions = oldLeaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions + 1\n\t}\n\n\t// update the lock itself\n\tif err = le.config.Lock.Update(ctx, leaderElectionRecord); err != nil {\n\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Failed to update lock\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\n\tle.setObservedRecord(&leaderElectionRecord)\n\treturn true\n}\n\n// tryAcquireOrRenew tries to acquire a leader lease if it is not already acquired,\n// else it tries to renew the lease if it has already been acquired. Returns true\n// on success else returns false.\nfunc (le *LeaderElector) tryAcquireOrRenew(ctx context.Context) bool {\n\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n\tnow := metav1.NewTime(le.clock.Now())\n\tleaderElectionRecord := rl.LeaderElectionRecord{\n\t\tHolderIdentity:       le.config.Lock.Identity(),\n\t\tLeaseDurationSeconds: int(le.config.LeaseDuration / time.Second),\n\t\tRenewTime:            now,\n\t\tAcquireTime:          now,\n\t}\n\n\t// 1. fast path for the leader to update optimistically assuming that the record observed\n\t// last time is the current version.\n\tif le.IsLeader() && le.isLeaseValid(now.Time) {\n\t\toldObservedRecord := le.getObservedRecord()\n\t\tleaderElectionRecord.AcquireTime = oldObservedRecord.AcquireTime\n\t\tleaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions = oldObservedRecord.LeaderTransitions\n\n\t\terr := le.config.Lock.Update(ctx, leaderElectionRecord)\n\t\tif err == nil {\n\t\t\tle.setObservedRecord(&leaderElectionRecord)\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t}\n\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Failed to update lease optimistically, falling back to slow path\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\n\t}\n\n\t// 2. obtain or create the ElectionRecord\n\toldLeaderElectionRecord, oldLeaderElectionRawRecord, err := le.config.Lock.Get(ctx)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\tif !errors.IsNotFound(err) {\n\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Error retrieving lease lock\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t\tif err = le.config.Lock.Create(ctx, leaderElectionRecord); err != nil {\n\t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Error initially creating lease lock\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tle.setObservedRecord(&leaderElectionRecord)\n\n\t\treturn true\n\t}\n\n\t// 3. Record obtained, check the Identity & Time\n\tif !bytes.Equal(le.observedRawRecord, oldLeaderElectionRawRecord) {\n\t\tle.setObservedRecord(oldLeaderElectionRecord)\n\n\t\tle.observedRawRecord = oldLeaderElectionRawRecord\n\t}\n\tif len(oldLeaderElectionRecord.HolderIdentity) > 0 && le.isLeaseValid(now.Time) && !le.IsLeader() {\n\t\tlogger.V(4).Info(\"Lease is held by and has not yet expired\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe(), \"holder\", oldLeaderElectionRecord.HolderIdentity)\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\n\t// 4. We're going to try to update. The leaderElectionRecord is set to it's default\n\t// here. Let's correct it before updating.\n\tif le.IsLeader() {\n\t\tleaderElectionRecord.AcquireTime = oldLeaderElectionRecord.AcquireTime\n\t\tleaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions = oldLeaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions\n\t\tle.metrics.slowpathExercised(le.config.Name)\n\t} else {\n\t\tleaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions = oldLeaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions + 1\n\t}\n\n\t// update the lock itself\n\tif err = le.config.Lock.Update(ctx, leaderElectionRecord); err != nil {\n\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Failed to update lease\", \"lock\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\n\tle.setObservedRecord(&leaderElectionRecord)\n\treturn true\n}\n\nfunc (le *LeaderElector) maybeReportTransition() {\n\tif le.observedRecord.HolderIdentity == le.reportedLeader {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\tle.reportedLeader = le.observedRecord.HolderIdentity\n\tif le.config.Callbacks.OnNewLeader != nil {\n\t\tgo le.config.Callbacks.OnNewLeader(le.reportedLeader)\n\t}\n}\n\n// Check will determine if the current lease is expired by more than timeout.\nfunc (le *LeaderElector) Check(maxTolerableExpiredLease time.Duration) error {\n\tif !le.IsLeader() {\n\t\t// Currently not concerned with the case that we are hot standby\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\t// If we are more than timeout seconds after the lease duration that is past the timeout\n\t// on the lease renew. Time to start reporting ourselves as unhealthy. We should have\n\t// died but conditions like deadlock can prevent this. (See #70819)\n\tle.observedRecordLock.RLock()\n\tlastObservation := le.observedTime\n\tleaseDuration := le.config.LeaseDuration\n\tle.observedRecordLock.RUnlock()\n\n\tif le.clock.Since(lastObservation) > leaseDuration+maxTolerableExpiredLease {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"failed election to renew leadership on lease %s\", le.config.Name)\n\t}\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\nfunc (le *LeaderElector) isLeaseValid(now time.Time) bool {\n\t// Lock to safely read both the time and the record\n\tle.observedRecordLock.RLock()\n\tdefer le.observedRecordLock.RUnlock()\n\n\treturn le.observedTime.Add(time.Second * time.Duration(le.observedRecord.LeaseDurationSeconds)).After(now)\n}\n\n// setObservedRecord will set a new observedRecord and update observedTime to the current time.\n// Protect critical sections with lock.\nfunc (le *LeaderElector) setObservedRecord(observedRecord *rl.LeaderElectionRecord) {\n\tle.observedRecordLock.Lock()\n\tdefer le.observedRecordLock.Unlock()\n\n\tle.observedRecord = *observedRecord\n\tle.observedTime = le.clock.Now()\n}\n\n// getObservedRecord returns observersRecord.\n// Protect critical sections with lock.\nfunc (le *LeaderElector) getObservedRecord() rl.LeaderElectionRecord {\n\tle.observedRecordLock.RLock()\n\tdefer le.observedRecordLock.RUnlock()\n\n\treturn le.observedRecord\n}\n","numLines":562,"startLine":1,"totalLines":562}}}

\"Resign\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"## Kubernetes Lease-Based Leader Election\\n\\nKubernetes implements leader election using a **lease-based approach** with periodic renewal, as seen in the client-go library and Kubernetes control plane controllers.\\n\\n### Architecture\\nThe implementation consists of three layers:\\n\\n1. **Resource Lock Layer** (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/`): Abstracts the storage backend for leader election records. The `Interface` defines Get/Create/Update operations, with `LeaseLock` implementing these using the Kubernetes Lease API (coordination.k8s.io/v1). A `LeaderElectionRecord` is stored in the Lease spec, containing HolderIdentity, AcquireTime, RenewTime, LeaseDurationSeconds, and LeaderTransitions.\\n\\n2. **Leader Elector Layer** (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`): The main `LeaderElector` orchestrates the election process. The `Run()` method starts the election loop, calling `acquire()` to gain leadership and `renew()` to maintain it. The `tryAcquireOrRenew()` function implements a fast-path for incumbents (checking locally cached lease validity) and a slow-path for challengers (fetching from API server). Leadership changes trigger `OnStartedLeading`/`OnStoppedLeading` callbacks.\\n\\n3. **Controller Layer** (`pkg/controlplane/controller/leaderelection/`): Kubernetes components integrate leader election with controller logic. The `leaderelection_controller.go` coordinates leader election for components, while `leasecandidate.go` implements coordinated leader election with version-based candidate promotion (ALPHA feature).\\n\\n### Failover and Re-election Mechanism\\n- **Lease Duration**: The `LeaseDuration` (typically 15s) defines how long a non-leader must wait before attempting to take over after the incumbent's last renewal.\\n- **Renewal**: The leader continuously calls `renew()`, which polls every `RetryPeriod` (typically 2s) until `RenewDeadline` (typically 10s).\\n- **Failover**: When the incumbent crashes or fails to renew, the lease naturally expires. Any non-leader can then call `tryAcquireOrRenew()` to acquire the lease by updating it with their identity.\\n- **Clock Tolerance**: The implementation uses local timestamps only, tolerating arbitrary clock skew by waiting for RenewDeadline periods.\\n- **Transitions**: `LeaderTransitions` counter tracks leadership changes for monitoring.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## etcd Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd implements leader election using the **Raft consensus algorithm** for internal cluster leadership, complemented by a client-facing election API based on leases.\\n\\n### Internal Raft-Based Architecture\\n\\nThe Raft layer (`server/etcdserver/raft.go`, `server/etcdserver/server.go`) manages cluster leader election:\\n\\n1. **Raft Node** (`raftNode`): Runs the Raft state machine in a dedicated goroutine. The `start()` method monitors `r.Ready()` channels, which emit raft.Ready structs containing state changes, committed entries, and messages.\\n\\n2. **Leader State Tracking**: When Raft detects a leader change via `rd.SoftState.Lead`, the `raftReadyHandler` callbacks update the EtcdServer:\\n   - `updateLead()` via `setLead()` atomically stores the new leader ID\\n   - `updateLeadership()` handles role-specific logic: demoting lessor and pausing compactor on followers, resuming them on leaders\\n   - `leaderChanged.Notify()` signals leader changes\\n\\n3. **Failover Mechanism**: Raft automatically holds elections when:\\n   - Followers don't receive heartbeats (within `heartbeat` interval)\\n   - Candidates increment their term and send RequestVote RPCs\\n   - The first node to gain a majority becomes leader\\n   - This is detected via `rd.RaftState == raft.StateLeader`\\n\\n### Client-Facing Election API\\n\\netcd exposes a higher-level election API for applications:\\n\\n1. **Session Layer** (`client/v3/concurrency/session.go`): Creates a lease-backed session with automatic keep-alive. Sessions use `client.KeepAlive()` to maintain liveness.\\n\\n2. **Election Primitives** (`client/v3/concurrency/election.go`):\\n   - `Campaign(ctx, val)`: Atomically creates a key at `keyPrefix/{leaseID}` with a compare-and-swap transaction. If already created, waits for lower-revision keys to be deleted via `waitDeletes()`, implementing a queue-based election.\\n   - `Proclaim(ctx, val)`: Updates the value without re-election, conditional on key revision matching.\\n   - `Resign(ctx)`: Deletes the leader key, triggering the next candidate.\\n   - `Leader(ctx)`: Queries the current leader (first key by creation revision).\\n   - `Observe(ctx)`: Streams leader changes via watching and comparing create revisions.\\n\\n3. **Server-Side gRPC API** (`server/etcdserver/api/v3election/election.go`): The `electionServer` adapts protobuf messages to the concurrency election primitives, exposing Campaign, Proclaim, Resign, Leader, and Observe operations.\\n\\n### Failover and Re-election in etcd\\n\\n**At the Raft layer**: Failover is automatic via Raft timeouts:\\n- If the leader becomes unavailable, followers timeout and become candidates\\n- Candidates send RequestVote to peers; the first to win a majority becomes leader\\n- The Raft term counter ensures safety: stale leaders are rejected\\n- Detected via `rd.SoftState.Lead` transitioning to `raft.None` and back\\n\\n**At the application layer**: Election re-campaigns when:\\n- The lease expires (session keep-alive fails)\\n- The leader explicitly resigns\\n- Candidates wait for all higher-revision keys to be deleted before becoming leader\\n\\n### Comparison\\n\\n**Kubernetes**: Uses optimistic lease renewal with periodic polling. Simple, stateless, but requires API server availability and tolerates clock skew.\\n\\n**etcd**: Uses Raft for automatic, byzantine-fault-tolerant cluster consensus. More complex but ensures strong consistency and automatic failover without external coordination. The client election API layered on top provides similar semantics to Kubernetes but with stronger guarantees.\\n\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1224,"cache_read_input_tokens":64292,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1224},"output_tokens":2,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"04f00702-fa2c-403f-887f-3d6d1003ffda","uuid":"8f46a48c-b17e-475c-9b4c-75a18b3036a4"}

\"Resign\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"## Kubernetes Lease-Based Leader Election\\n\\nKubernetes implements leader election using a **lease-based approach** with periodic renewal, as seen in the client-go library and Kubernetes control plane controllers.\\n\\n### Architecture\\nThe implementation consists of three layers:\\n\\n1. **Resource Lock Layer** (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/`): Abstracts the storage backend for leader election records. The `Interface` defines Get/Create/Update operations, with `LeaseLock` implementing these using the Kubernetes Lease API (coordination.k8s.io/v1). A `LeaderElectionRecord` is stored in the Lease spec, containing HolderIdentity, AcquireTime, RenewTime, LeaseDurationSeconds, and LeaderTransitions.\\n\\n2. **Leader Elector Layer** (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`): The main `LeaderElector` orchestrates the election process. The `Run()` method starts the election loop, calling `acquire()` to gain leadership and `renew()` to maintain it. The `tryAcquireOrRenew()` function implements a fast-path for incumbents (checking locally cached lease validity) and a slow-path for challengers (fetching from API server). Leadership changes trigger `OnStartedLeading`/`OnStoppedLeading` callbacks.\\n\\n3. **Controller Layer** (`pkg/controlplane/controller/leaderelection/`): Kubernetes components integrate leader election with controller logic. The `leaderelection_controller.go` coordinates leader election for components, while `leasecandidate.go` implements coordinated leader election with version-based candidate promotion (ALPHA feature).\\n\\n### Failover and Re-election Mechanism\\n- **Lease Duration**: The `LeaseDuration` (typically 15s) defines how long a non-leader must wait before attempting to take over after the incumbent's last renewal.\\n- **Renewal**: The leader continuously calls `renew()`, which polls every `RetryPeriod` (typically 2s) until `RenewDeadline` (typically 10s).\\n- **Failover**: When the incumbent crashes or fails to renew, the lease naturally expires. Any non-leader can then call `tryAcquireOrRenew()` to acquire the lease by updating it with their identity.\\n- **Clock Tolerance**: The implementation uses local timestamps only, tolerating arbitrary clock skew by waiting for RenewDeadline periods.\\n- **Transitions**: `LeaderTransitions` counter tracks leadership changes for monitoring.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## etcd Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd implements leader election using the **Raft consensus algorithm** for internal cluster leadership, complemented by a client-facing election API based on leases.\\n\\n### Internal Raft-Based Architecture\\n\\nThe Raft layer (`server/etcdserver/raft.go`, `server/etcdserver/server.go`) manages cluster leader election:\\n\\n1. **Raft Node** (`raftNode`): Runs the Raft state machine in a dedicated goroutine. The `start()` method monitors `r.Ready()` channels, which emit raft.Ready structs containing state changes, committed entries, and messages.\\n\\n2. **Leader State Tracking**: When Raft detects a leader change via `rd.SoftState.Lead`, the `raftReadyHandler` callbacks update the EtcdServer:\\n   - `updateLead()` via `setLead()` atomically stores the new leader ID\\n   - `updateLeadership()` handles role-specific logic: demoting lessor and pausing compactor on followers, resuming them on leaders\\n   - `leaderChanged.Notify()` signals leader changes\\n\\n3. **Failover Mechanism**: Raft automatically holds elections when:\\n   - Followers don't receive heartbeats (within `heartbeat` interval)\\n   - Candidates increment their term and send RequestVote RPCs\\n   - The first node to gain a majority becomes leader\\n   - This is detected via `rd.RaftState == raft.StateLeader`\\n\\n### Client-Facing Election API\\n\\netcd exposes a higher-level election API for applications:\\n\\n1. **Session Layer** (`client/v3/concurrency/session.go`): Creates a lease-backed session with automatic keep-alive. Sessions use `client.KeepAlive()` to maintain liveness.\\n\\n2. **Election Primitives** (`client/v3/concurrency/election.go`):\\n   - `Campaign(ctx, val)`: Atomically creates a key at `keyPrefix/{leaseID}` with a compare-and-swap transaction. If already created, waits for lower-revision keys to be deleted via `waitDeletes()`, implementing a queue-based election.\\n   - `Proclaim(ctx, val)`: Updates the value without re-election, conditional on key revision matching.\\n   - `Resign(ctx)`: Deletes the leader key, triggering the next candidate.\\n   - `Leader(ctx)`: Queries the current leader (first key by creation revision).\\n   - `Observe(ctx)`: Streams leader changes via watching and comparing create revisions.\\n\\n3. **Server-Side gRPC API** (`server/etcdserver/api/v3election/election.go`): The `electionServer` adapts protobuf messages to the concurrency election primitives, exposing Campaign, Proclaim, Resign, Leader, and Observe operations.\\n\\n### Failover and Re-election in etcd\\n\\n**At the Raft layer**: Failover is automatic via Raft timeouts:\\n- If the leader becomes unavailable, followers timeout and become candidates\\n- Candidates send RequestVote to peers; the first to win a majority becomes leader\\n- The Raft term counter ensures safety: stale leaders are rejected\\n- Detected via `rd.SoftState.Lead` transitioning to `raft.None` and back\\n\\n**At the application layer**: Election re-campaigns when:\\n- The lease expires (session keep-alive fails)\\n- The leader explicitly resigns\\n- Candidates wait for all higher-revision keys to be deleted before becoming leader\\n\\n### Comparison\\n\\n**Kubernetes**: Uses optimistic lease renewal with periodic polling. Simple, stateless, but requires API server availability and tolerates clock skew.\\n\\n**etcd**: Uses Raft for automatic, byzantine-fault-tolerant cluster consensus. More complex but ensures strong consistency and automatic failover without external coordination. The client election API layered on top provides similar semantics to Kubernetes but with stronger guarantees.\\n\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Here are the key findings:\n\n### Kubernetes: Lease-Based Leader Election\n- **Location**: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/`\n- **Core Components**:\n  - `LeaderElector`: Main orchestrator with `Run()`, `acquire()`, and `renew()` methods\n  - `LeaseLock`: Implements the Kubernetes Lease API for storing election state\n  - `LeaderElectionRecord`: Stores holder identity, timestamps, and transition counts\n  - `LeaseCandidate`: New ALPHA coordinated election with version-based promotion\n\n- **Failover Strategy**: \n  - Non-leaders wait for `LeaseDuration` (typically 15s) after incumbent's last renewal\n  - Periodic polling with `RetryPeriod` (typically 2s)\n  - Tolerates arbitrary clock skew using local timestamps only\n\n### etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\n- **Internal Layer**: `server/etcdserver/raft.go` and `server.go`\n  - `raftNode`: Runs Raft state machine, monitors leader state changes\n  - `EtcdServer`: Handles leadership transitions via `setLead()` and callbacks\n  - Automatic failover when heartbeats timeout\n\n- **Client API Layer**: `client/v3/concurrency/election.go`\n  - `Election`: Provides Campaign, Proclaim, Resign, Leader, Observe primitives\n  - `Session`: Lease-backed session with automatic keep-alive\n  - Queue-based election using key creation revisions\n\n- **Failover Strategy**:\n  - Raft: Automatic election when leader unavailable (consensus-based)\n  - Application: Campaign waits for higher-revision keys to be deleted\n\nThe analysis shows Kubernetes uses stateless, optimistic lease renewal while etcd uses byzantine-fault-tolerant Raft consensus for cluster leadership with a layered election API for applications.\n\nThe complete analysis has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`."}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1136,"cache_read_input_tokens":70205,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1136},"output_tokens":5,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"04f00702-fa2c-403f-887f-3d6d1003ffda","uuid":"7c729adc-2f89-4ffb-8214-c03d84073961"}
